<div id="review_1155395207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1155395207" />
    <a title="Stephen Arvidson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38585870-stephen-arvidson"><img alt="Stephen Arvidson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469994519p2/38585870.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1155395207?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen Arvidson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen Arvidson" href="/user/show/38585870-stephen-arvidson">Stephen Arvidson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440242864" href="/book/show/387511.Hannibal_Rising">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38585870-stephen-arvidson?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38585870-stephen-arvidson?shelf=hannibal-lecter">hannibal-lecter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38585870-stephen-arvidson?shelf=cannibalism">cannibalism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38585870-stephen-arvidson?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38585870-stephen-arvidson?shelf=bildungsroman">bildungsroman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38585870-stephen-arvidson?shelf=france">france</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1155395207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7682097031710109693">While not as satisfying as <i>Red Dragon</i>, <i>Silence of the Lambs</i>, or (to a lesser extent) <i>Hannibal</i>, Thomas Harris manages to cook up a decadent appetizer to an already loaded three-course meal. It's hard not to see <i>Hannibal Rising</i> as a last-ditch effort to revive an ailing franchise by further developing one of the most complex characters of modern fiction. By offering a traumatic origin story as explanation for how a human being could become Dr. Lecter, Harris walks a dangerous tightrope in making h</span>
  <span id="freeText7682097031710109693" style="display:none">While not as satisfying as <i>Red Dragon</i>, <i>Silence of the Lambs</i>, or (to a lesser extent) <i>Hannibal</i>, Thomas Harris manages to cook up a decadent appetizer to an already loaded three-course meal. It's hard not to see <i>Hannibal Rising</i> as a last-ditch effort to revive an ailing franchise by further developing one of the most complex characters of modern fiction. By offering a traumatic origin story as explanation for how a human being could become Dr. Lecter, Harris walks a dangerous tightrope in making his magnificent creation a less-fascinating avatar of evil.<br /><br />What this novel gives readers is a sumptuous look at Hannibal's youth, the plot of which is not much more than a thrilling story of grisly vengeance. A young Lithuanian aristocrat loses his parents and darling sister, Mischa, in the final desperate days of World War II. Hannibal is forced to watch as little Mischa is devoured by callous Nazi-sympathizing ruffians whom Hannibal later tracks down and gruesomely dispatches in the natural course of the novel. By the end of <i>Hannibal Rising</i>, the reader is left with a better understanding of the epicurean psychiatrist, even if the book doesn't exactly conclude with the satisfaction one would wish from an examination of Lecter's tenebrous beginnings. The action is swift and often fleeting, and the chapters brief (often only four pages), and the sentences are, for the most part, simplistic and lacking the eloquence found in Harris's preceding works. The dialogue is occasionally stilted and the character of Lady Murasaki, who sensually introduces the impressionable teenage Hannibal to a rarified world of Japanese art and poetry, exists only to be beautiful.<br /><br />Thankfully, Hannibal Lecter remains a preeminent literary icon, a dominant fictional boogeyman, and that's primarily due to Anthony Hopkins's unforgettable screen incarnation. <i>Hannibal Rising</i> reads like the novelization of a screenplay; not surprisingly Thomas Harris wrote the screenplay in the course of writing this novel. That isn't to say the book is a complete loss, for even after so many years since writing <i>Red Dragon</i> and <i>Silence</i>, Harris still possesses a keen aptitude for depicting the animal nature that lurks beneath mankind's veneer of civilization.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7682097031710109693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7FQV3Z/ycbA5OSGG400O7/Cg6jiJyROL1mqvmOLMKHPWcnwPJKy42J4SlecUuAQwJv8N8EdEneyNFOkpL4/a6Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_13092938'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13092938-the-season-to-be-wary?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Season to Be Wary<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/95125.Rod_Serling?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Rod Serling<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.27 avg rating &mdash; 82 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1967\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer2261706137741356655\">In the so-called \"Golden Age\" of live television drama in the middle fifties, the name Rod Serling appeared regularly on the ward lists. Winner of six Emmys (he was nominated nine times), two Sylvania Awards, on Peabody Award, and one Christopher Awa<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2261706137741356655\" style=\"display:none\">In the so-called &quot;Golden Age&quot; of live television drama in the middle fifties, the name Rod Serling appeared regularly on the ward lists. Winner of six Emmys (he was nominated nine times), two Sylvania Awards, on Peabody Award, and one Christopher Award for his teleplays, Serling came as close as anyone to dominating an era that abounded with talented men. His plays &quot;Requiem for a Heavyweight&quot; and &quot;Patterns&quot; are usually the first items on the lips of television aficionados reminiscing about the good old days. Yet as television changed, Rod Serling kept pace. He became producer and chief writer for the famous &quot;Twilight Zone&quot; series. These bizarre and fantastic adventures into the occult and demonic were without doubt one of the most creative, imaginative and successful enterprises in the history of television.\nNow Rod Serling has applied his prodigious writing talents to a new medium: one in which he is perhaps destined to make his greatest mark. The three novellas that compromise THE SEASON TO BE WARY betray the skillful hand of a master storyteller and prose stylist. Fired with a savage yet disciplined irony, paced with deliberate cadence that rises to a starting denouement, each story explores the theme of a terrible vengeance delivered for terrible deeds performed.\nIn &quot;The Escape Route,&quot; ex-Gruppenfuehrer Joseph Strobe - ex-deputy assistant commander of Auschwitz, ex-confidant of Heinrich Himmler - putters about his little rathole in Buenos Aires chewing over the good times he had breaking Jews. Yet his snug little world is turned upside down b the capture of Adolf Eichmann, and Strobe soon finds himself on the wrong end of a terrifying hunt.\n&quot;Color Scheme&quot; recounts the life and times of the great King Connacher, racist and rabble-rouser, who makes his living on the stump, preaching the lynching gospel, only to find himself one summer evening the victim of an extraordinary case of mistaken identity.\nIn &quot;Eyes,&quot; Miss Claudia Menlo, who in her fifty lifeless years has been denied nothing that she wanted - except her sight - manipulates people with the same purposeful indifference with which she fondles the expensive bric-a-brac in her lavishly cluttered dwelling. Yet her insistant will is brutally thwarted by the one set of circumstances she cannot control.\nSerling has infused these simple, forceful tales with an extraordinary richness of character and detail. There is, for example, the Prussian officer Gruber, who cannot stomach the pigs like Strobe he helped create and with whom he is forced to share his guilt. And there is Indian Charlie Hatcher, the most memorable portrait of a burned-out prizefighter since Serling\'s own justly famous Mountain Rivera.\nThe power, the drive, the complexity and subtlety of these novellas mark Rod Serling as one of the most important and graceful fiction writers. Mr. Serling is a graduate of Antioch College and lives in Southern California with his wife and two children.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2261706137741356655\" href=\"#\" <span id="freeTextContainer4703938181633182009"><i>Librarian Note:<br/>There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Thomas Harris began his writing career covering crime in the United States and Mexico, and was a reporter and editor for the Associated Press in New York City. His first novel, <i>Black Sunday</i>, was printed in 1975, followed by <i>Red Dragon</i> in 1981, <i>The Silence of the Lambs</i> in 1988, <i>Hannibal</i> in 1999, and <i>Hannibal Risin</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4703938181633182009" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note:<br />There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Thomas Harris began his writing career covering crime in the United States and Mexico, and was a reporter and editor for the Associated Press in New York City. His first novel, <i>Black Sunday</i>, was printed in 1975, followed by <i>Red Dragon</i> in 1981, <i>The Silence of the Lambs</i> in 1988, <i>Hannibal</i> in 1999, and <i>Hannibal Rising</i> in 2006.</span>
